<div id="review_73328074" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73328074" />
    <a title="Shaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1241668-shaya"><img alt="Shaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219282693p2/1241668.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73328074?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaya" href="/user/show/1241668-shaya">Shaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">middle-schoolers who want more books like The Giver</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1241668-shaya?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1241668-shaya?shelf=school-year-2009-2010">school-year-2009-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73328074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7296245909609561260">The Other Side of the Island is reasonably intersting but lacking a little in character development and surprises in the plot. It has some ideas to reflect on about what our values and what we see as problems in the world. <br/><br/>One thing that distinguishes The Other Side of the Island from other dystopian stories is that this is clearly set after the World suffers some of the effects of global warming. This aspect makes the story seem a bit more relevant and possible. Another distinguishing aspect is</span>
  <span id="freeText7296245909609561260" style="display:none">The Other Side of the Island is reasonably intersting but lacking a little in character development and surprises in the plot. It has some ideas to reflect on about what our values and what we see as problems in the world. <br /><br />One thing that distinguishes The Other Side of the Island from other dystopian stories is that this is clearly set after the World suffers some of the effects of global warming. This aspect makes the story seem a bit more relevant and possible. Another distinguishing aspect is that words that are common in our world are used with a different shade of meaning. The controlling leader of the Colonies uses words like Accept, Mother Earth, Safe and Secure as descriptors of Her perfect society. Words like Rejector, Enemy of Nature, Hijacker, Trespasser, etc. are used to describe those against the controlling Corporation. But these were the "good guys" in the story. I thought it was interesting to think about what the words really mean and how they can be represent positive and negative ideas depending on who is using them and how. <br /><br />And I did like the message that our human wish for safety can harm us.<br /><br />I liked the development of the main character, Honor. She starts out willing to dissent like her parents do but then gets squashed into wanting to conform because there is so much pressure to. I never felt like I got to know any of the characters inside and out. They did change but they were a little too cardboard for my taste. The third person narration contributed to that. <br /><br />The plot was pretty predictable. It fit the template of dystopian novels. <br /><br />It felt a lot like The Giver by Lois Lowry. And I've also read The Silenced by James DeVita in the same genre. Of the three The Giver is the best written. I thought The Silenced was very haunting. I still think of certain images from it today, a year after I read it. The Other Side of the Island has a world where it's easy to see how we got from where we are to there. But I'd recommend the other two over this book. <br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7296245909609561260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5811096925736568546">Ten year old Honor and her mother and father have just been forcibly relocated to an island in the Tranquil Sea from their home in the Northern Islands. When Honor is being interviewed for her place in school, the headmistress stresses that her name is not Acceptable since the H is silent. Honor struggles to fit in while her parents secretly join the Forecasters, a group of rebels who want to displace Earth Mother who is bent on Enclosure - ceiling the islands against the onslaught of Weather. W</span>
  <span id="freeText5811096925736568546" style="display:none">Ten year old Honor and her mother and father have just been forcibly relocated to an island in the Tranquil Sea from their home in the Northern Islands. When Honor is being interviewed for her place in school, the headmistress stresses that her name is not Acceptable since the H is silent. Honor struggles to fit in while her parents secretly join the Forecasters, a group of rebels who want to displace Earth Mother who is bent on Enclosure - ceiling the islands against the onslaught of Weather. When Honor's parents have a second child and choose to keep him, Honor feels that she must take action to help the family become part of society. Her first step is to take the name Heloise, which has a pronounced H. Unfortunately, this is what spurs the authorities to Disappear the parents. Now Honor and her brother Quintilion are orphans and must live in the Boarding Home. Her one friend Helix lets her in on a secret - the Orderlies, vapid, staring creatures who do all the work are Disappeared parents. Together Honor and Helix embark on a plan to find their parents and escape Earth Mother's control. This is another dystopian book that I hoped to enjoy more than I did. I did like the description of the society created by Earth Mother but Honor was not a sympathetic character and was more of a brat. I also wanted to know how the tree octopus Octavio fit into the story. He was there and gone too fast. The author never really explained his connection to Honor. It does sound like a sequel could come along.</span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781595141965" href="/book/show/6363971-the-other-side-of-the-island">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3491365-kristin-mybookishways-reviews?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130310470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6404655343286122582">Well, we’ve finally gone and pissed off Mother Earth. We finally mucked up the planet enough and The Flood was sent to put us in our place. Never fear, because the Corporation and the Earth Mother are here to save the day! “The Other Side of the Island” by Allegra Goodman takes place in the eighteenth year of Enclosure (where it’s always sunny and green under the dome), long after Mother Earth dumped on us in the form of the Flood. This is Honor’s story (silent H, which is a no-no, since she was</span>
  <span id="freeText6404655343286122582" style="display:none">Well, we’ve finally gone and pissed off Mother Earth. We finally mucked up the planet enough and The Flood was sent to put us in our place. Never fear, because the Corporation and the Earth Mother are here to save the day! “The Other Side of the Island” by Allegra Goodman takes place in the eighteenth year of Enclosure (where it’s always sunny and green under the dome), long after Mother Earth dumped on us in the form of the Flood. This is Honor’s story (silent H, which is a no-no, since she was born in an H year, and, you know, we should be able to hear that H). Her name alone already gives you a good idea of Honor’s parents and their subversive ways. I’m not going to dance around it; this book is depressing. Allegra’s family is forced to move to Island 365 from the North (a wild place and full of Partisans-dissenters) by the Corporation, and thus begins the gradual muting of her world’s colors and the end of her family’s personal freedom. I love Ms. Goodman’s use of dark humor here, especially when reading excerpts from their “educational” pamphlets. It’s a life full of structure, propaganda, and everything and everyone in its place, and the story is told in a fairly straightforward, uncomplicated manner, and it really works here. The Corporation reminds me of my Homeowner’s Association except I haven’t known them to “disappear” anyone’s parents for not keeping the weeds out of the tree well. At least not yet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6404655343286122582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_50620012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50620012" />
    <a title="Abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/638271-abby"><img alt="Abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451777675p2/638271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50620012?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby" href="/user/show/638271-abby">Abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/638271-abby?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/638271-abby?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/638271-abby?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50620012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14499568178501950864">3.5 stars. A satisfying, well-written addition to the ever-expanding category of YA dystopian fiction with an environmental twist. In this story, the earth's continents have been reduced to islands by the catastrophic effects of global warming, and Big Brother = Earth Mother, the seemingly benevolent leader who rules the "safe" and "secure" Colonies, where she's trying to establish New Weather and a new, authoritarian society "for the good of the planet." Ten-year-old Honor has recently moved to</span>
  <span id="freeText14499568178501950864" style="display:none">3.5 stars. A satisfying, well-written addition to the ever-expanding category of YA dystopian fiction with an environmental twist. In this story, the earth's continents have been reduced to islands by the catastrophic effects of global warming, and Big Brother = Earth Mother, the seemingly benevolent leader who rules the "safe" and "secure" Colonies, where she's trying to establish New Weather and a new, authoritarian society "for the good of the planet." Ten-year-old Honor has recently moved to the Colonies from the Northern Islands, with her parents, Will and Pamela, who are less than model citizens in the eyes of Earth Mother and her minions. Desperate to fit in, Honor makes a seemingly innocent choice that has severe consequences for her family -- and leads her to discover what's hidden on the other side of the island.<br /><br />Goodman captures perfectly the dismay that a child craving security and stability feels when her parents do not follow community norms and her sense of being an outsider is amplified -- so even though some readers may be frustrated by some of Honor's actions, she remains a sympathetic character. I'm only giving it 3.5 stars though because it's not really dark enough for a dystopian novel in my opinion -- even a teen dystopian novel. But it does have a scary librarian so it gets points for that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14499568178501950864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_101472076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101472076" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101472076?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101472076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4893666353984787652">The Other Side of the Island gives up a stark picture of the future when evolving science and paranoia meld together to create a society ruled under utmost Totalitarianism.<br/><br/>Wow, some of the stuff the author thought up in here was pretty wicked. The concept of this book is fantastic and thoroughly developed. Some of the plot twists were predictable and others weren’t. The characters, especially Honor, were realistic with plenty of room for growth, and had their own vices and flaws.<br/><br/>The pacing of th</span>
  <span id="freeText4893666353984787652" style="display:none">The Other Side of the Island gives up a stark picture of the future when evolving science and paranoia meld together to create a society ruled under utmost Totalitarianism.<br /><br />Wow, some of the stuff the author thought up in here was pretty wicked. The concept of this book is fantastic and thoroughly developed. Some of the plot twists were predictable and others weren’t. The characters, especially Honor, were realistic with plenty of room for growth, and had their own vices and flaws.<br /><br />The pacing of the book was slow but when the real escape/break the mold/rescue plot rush to the climax appeared at the halfway point I couldn’t put it down. If there was one thing that dragged this down was the writing. It felt stiff, choppy, and utilized a lot of repetition, and short sentences. Not my type of style.<br /><br />I liked how the story grew with the character and the different phases of life she went through. The friendships between her and Helix was cute although later on I thought it was a bit abrupt that she got back into his friendly graces so soon.<br /><br />I’m not sure about the ending though. It’s either you hate it and think it was a deliberately done cop out, or fantastic because of the leeway it gives you to think up your own ending. Whatever the case is, I enjoyed this book, and would recommend it someone who wants some lighter dystopian fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4893666353984787652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1624931-katie?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer259246465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9758839921582125419">Global warming has caused the polar ice caps to melt and sea levels to rise; consequently, much of the Earth’s land has disappeared, leaving only high-lying islands. A corporation run by a woman known as Earth Mother now rules all of the islands. Honor and her family have moved to Island 365, and from the outset it looks like they’ll have a hard time fitting in. First of all, Honor’s name is all wrong. Everyone born in her year has a name that begins with H, but Honor’s name has a silent H and i</span>
  <span id="freeText9758839921582125419" style="display:none">Global warming has caused the polar ice caps to melt and sea levels to rise; consequently, much of the Earth’s land has disappeared, leaving only high-lying islands. A corporation run by a woman known as Earth Mother now rules all of the islands. Honor and her family have moved to Island 365, and from the outset it looks like they’ll have a hard time fitting in. First of all, Honor’s name is all wrong. Everyone born in her year has a name that begins with H, but Honor’s name has a silent H and is therefore all wrong. Honor’s family also sings songs (forbidden), stays out past curfew (a serious offense), and worst of all, has a second child. Honor grows more and more embarrassed by her family’s disrespect of the rules, but her embarrassment turns to concern when she finds out what happens to people who do not fit in. [return][return]This book is similar to other futuristic children’s books, like the City of Ember books and the Shadow Children series. If you liked those books then you’ll probably like this one; however, it’s not a standout. I liked how some of Earth Mother’s rules were similar to the rules of the former Chinese ruler Mao Zedong, like how all people had to hang a picture of her in their house and have a book of her sayings. It is truly frightening how Earth Mother and the people who work for her are able to control the population.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9758839921582125419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_174004996" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174004996" />
    <a title="Karen Ball" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4310036-karen-ball"><img alt="Karen Ball" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297634861p2/4310036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174004996?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Ball" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Ball" href="/user/show/4310036-karen-ball">Karen Ball</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8158249-the-other-side-of-the-island">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174004996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1923921728115946400">Another dystopia! This one reminds me a lot of <i>The Giver</i>, but with a clearer setting, more information about how this place has come to be, and actually more realistic options for the people in the story. Honor and her parents have been reassigned to live on Island 365 in the Tranquil Sea. Her parents don't quite fit in, and neither does she in this extremely regulated place. In their first apartment, the Neighborhood Watch arrives to tell them that they are not allowed to sing Honor to sleep to</span>
  <span id="freeText1923921728115946400" style="display:none">Another dystopia! This one reminds me a lot of <i>The Giver</i>, but with a clearer setting, more information about how this place has come to be, and actually more realistic options for the people in the story. Honor and her parents have been reassigned to live on Island 365 in the Tranquil Sea. Her parents don't quite fit in, and neither does she in this extremely regulated place. In their first apartment, the Neighborhood Watch arrives to tell them that they are not allowed to sing Honor to sleep to make her feel better in this new place. Although the island is peaceful, it is difficult following the rules and being obedient to Earth Mother, the corporation that now runs the planet and regulates all life and events, including the weather. Honor meets Helix, who also is interested in more than what the people on the island are being offered. Slowly, Honor and Helix discover a horrible truth about life on the Island: one way or another, people who are unpredictable or different vanish, and they don't ever come back. This one is a good companion novel for The Giver in 6th grade, but also will work well with the Holocaust curriculum in 8th grade (the idea of controlled society, getting rid of those who are different, propaganda, etc). 6th grade and up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1923921728115946400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_53698095" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53698095" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1366723-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53698095?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/1366723-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53698095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1977836042100623702">This is another of those "scary future" worlds. Global warming has resulted in melted ice-cap, world-wide floods and destruction. As the book opens, one family has been "retrieved" from the north islands where they were basically hiding out, and assimilated into the current society of the southern islands. The government is under the control of Earth Mother who promises to protect and shield the planet from future destruction by use of weather control, and literal shields that stretch over the p</span>
  <span id="freeText1977836042100623702" style="display:none">This is another of those "scary future" worlds. Global warming has resulted in melted ice-cap, world-wide floods and destruction. As the book opens, one family has been "retrieved" from the north islands where they were basically hiding out, and assimilated into the current society of the southern islands. The government is under the control of Earth Mother who promises to protect and shield the planet from future destruction by use of weather control, and literal shields that stretch over the populated centers. Rebels are de-humanized through drugs that wipe out memory. And milder doses of this memory-erasing drug are used in all food stuffs and beverages to make the populace more pliable to Earth Mother's propaganda. The book's protagonist is Honor, who comes of age during the story, and must choose between the dangerous independence of her family tradition and the safe, acceptable patterns she is taught in school. The book is written fairly well, and Honor's dilemmas become very real and poignant. I guess I just get tired of "watch out, we're heading for trouble" books after awhile. But this one, for a young adult audience, is pretty good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1977836042100623702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1117835185" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1117835185" />
    <a title="Ange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5871271-ange"><img alt="Ange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589417026p2/5871271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1117835185?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ange" href="/user/show/5871271-ange">Ange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1117835185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3818178965254136362">I've loved quite a few post-apocalypse dystopian YA novels over the years, but I think this one will go down as one of my favorites. In a world where people live on domed islands in an attempt to satisfy the new government led by the figurehead of the Earth Mother, there are few who will question the rules for sustaining a safe and peaceful life. But Honor and her family are newcomers to this warm monitored environment. Now they are living in a southern island society where the rules and the agr</span>
  <span id="freeText3818178965254136362" style="display:none">I've loved quite a few post-apocalypse dystopian YA novels over the years, but I think this one will go down as one of my favorites. In a world where people live on domed islands in an attempt to satisfy the new government led by the figurehead of the Earth Mother, there are few who will question the rules for sustaining a safe and peaceful life. But Honor and her family are newcomers to this warm monitored environment. Now they are living in a southern island society where the rules and the agreed-upon realities are different from everything they know after having lived in a northern island. Their memories of snow and autumn leaves are things to hide and keep secret after being told by fellow society members that these memories are false and could not possibly have happened.<br /><br />I won't spoil the novel for you, but the ending is left wide open for questions for the reader to ask, and a choose-your-own-adventure prompt to decide what happens next to the characters and the world as they know it. I loved the way this book made me think and wonder and I highly recommend it to anyone who has ever questioned authority and/or marches to the beat of his/her own drum. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3818178965254136362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IEzalRGeX0lHK9U0UR6fv4wv5Al2zpTJ2LDpX3KtpcI8fODXkwLfKB7DC6azGVSYsMmhGG1U5mA9V0+pz/yK6A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BDjC0uSaQB1SRQt+494Ar7qEErRMIIEMX24DYKODV1AYCPiQZgbAfAut1ewB2cuIhmJXpVe686W6iaWWHtJ4eg==')})
  }

The governors of Florida, Texas, and North Carolina have all pledged that they will not spend taxpayer money subsidizing the liberal arts, and they seem to have an unlikely ally in President Obama. While at a General Electric plant in early 2014, Obama remarked, &quot;I promise you, folks can make a lot more, potentially, with skilled manufacturing or the trades than they might with an art history degree.&quot; These messages are hitting home: majors like English and history, once very popular and highly respected, are in steep decline.\n\n\n&quot;I get it,&quot; writes Fareed Zakaria, recalling the atmosphere in India where he grew up, which was even more obsessed with getting a skills-based education. However, the CNN host and best-selling author explains why this widely held view is mistaken and shortsighted.\n\n\nZakaria eloquently expounds on the virtues of a liberal arts education—how to write clearly, how to express yourself convincingly, and how to think analytically. He turns our leaders\' vocational argument on its head. American routine manufacturing jobs continue to get automated or outsourced, and specific vocational knowledge is often outdated within a few years. Engineering is a great profession, but key value-added skills you will also need are creativity, lateral thinking, design, communication, storytelling, and, more than anything, the ability to continually learn and enjoy learning—precisely the gifts of a liberal education.\n\n\nZakaria argues that technology is transforming education, opening up access to the best courses and classes in a vast variety of subjects for millions around the world. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15748643365808507251">Hello, Good Readers! It's a pleasure to meet you!<br/><br/>I was born in Brooklyn, but I grew up in Honolulu. When I was a seven year old living in Hawaii, I aspired to become a novelist--but I began by writing poetry and short stories.<br/><br/>In high school and college I focused on short stories and in June, 1986, I published my first in "Commentary." My first book was a collection of short stories, "Total Immersi</span>
  <span id="freeText15748643365808507251" style="display:none">Hello, Good Readers! It's a pleasure to meet you!<br /><br />I was born in Brooklyn, but I grew up in Honolulu. When I was a seven year old living in Hawaii, I aspired to become a novelist--but I began by writing poetry and short stories.<br /><br />In high school and college I focused on short stories and in June, 1986, I published my first in "Commentary." My first book was a collection of short stories, "Total Immersion." My second book, "The Family Markowitz" is a short story cycle that people tend to read as a novel.<br /><br />Much of my work is about family in its many forms. I am also interested in religion, science, the threats and opportunities of technology, and the exploration of islands, real, and imaginary. My novel, "Kaaterskill Falls" travels with a group of observant Jews to the Catskill Mountains. "Intuition" enters a research a lab, where a young post-doc makes a discovery that excites everybody except for one skeptic--his ex-girlfriend. A rare collection of cookbooks stars in my novel, "The Cookbook Collector." A girl named Honor tries to save her mother in my dystopian YA novel, "The Other Side of the Island."<br /><br />My newest novel "The Chalk Artist" tells the story of a young teacher, a chalk artist, and a boy fast disappearing into video games.<br /><br />If you'd like to learn more about me and about each of my books, check out my website:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://allegragoodman.com/">http://allegragoodman.com/</a><br /><br />or find me on Facebook: <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/AllegraGoodman">https://www.facebook.com/AllegraGoodman</a><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15748643365808507251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

When the wind was just right, the kites felt so strong and safe up there that Honor imagined nothing could budge them.<br /><br />'Ho bum," boasted Will, 'I could stand here all day and this kite would hold. It's like fishing.'<br /><br />'Fishing in reverse,' said Pamela. 'Sky fishing.'<br /><br />'What do you fish for in the air?' asked Honor.<br /><br />Pamela and Will started laughing. 'Oh, planets,' said Will. 'The occasional comet. An asteroid or two.'<br /><br />Honor held one kite string, and Will held the other. Pamela held Quintilian. On those afternoons, four did not seem like the wrong number for a family. Four seemed just right.&rdquo;</span>
